## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: classical mechanics — nonlinear oscillations / dynamical systems
**Analysis**: The target dv_dt is acceleration, and the available state variables are position x and velocity v with time t, which matches second-order ODE models for (possibly forced/damped) nonlinear oscillators. Common structures express dv_dt as a sum of restoring-force terms (functions of x), damping terms (functions of v), and external/parametric excitation (functions of t and sometimes x).

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Undamped linear oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x (simple harmonic restoring acceleration)
- Linear viscous damping + spring: dv_dt = -c0 * x + -c1 * v (mass-spring-damper in first-order state form)
- Constant bias / gravity-like offset: dv_dt = -c0 * x + c1 (equilibrium shift / constant forcing)
- Harmonic forcing: dv_dt = -c0 * x + -c1 * v + c2 * cos(c3 * t) (externally driven oscillator)
- General sinusoidal forcing (phase-complete): dv_dt = -c0 * x + -c1 * v + c2 * cos(c3 * t) + c4 * sin(c5 * t) (richer periodic drive)
- Duffing oscillator (cubic stiffness): dv_dt = -c0 * x + -c1 * x**3 + -c2 * v (hardening/softening nonlinear spring)
- Duffing with forcing: dv_dt = -c0 * x + -c1 * x**3 + -c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (canonical forced nonlinear oscillator)
- Pendulum-like (trigonometric restoring): dv_dt = -c0 * sin(c1 * x) + -c2 * v (finite-angle restoring force)
- Quadratic (aerodynamic) damping: dv_dt = -c0 * x + -c1 * v * Abs(v) (drag scaling with speed squared)
- Cubic damping: dv_dt = -c0 * x + -c1 * v**3 (strong nonlinear dissipation at large speeds)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x + c1 * (c2 + -x**2) * v (self-excited oscillation via negative damping near origin)
- Rayleigh oscillator form: dv_dt = -c0 * x + c1 * (c2 + -v**2) * v (velocity-dependent pumping and limiting)
- Parametric excitation (time-varying stiffness): dv_dt = -(c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x + -c3 * v (Mathieu-type parametric oscillator)
- Nonlinear stiffness with parametric modulation: dv_dt = -(c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x + -c3 * x**3 + -c4 * v (parametric Duffing oscillator)
- Amplitude-dependent frequency (effective stiffness): dv_dt = -(c0 + c1 * x**2) * x + -c2 * v (restoring term as x + x^3 grouped)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Restoring-force dominance (conservative core) → dv_dt primarily a function of x with odd symmetry (e.g., -c0*x, -c0*sin(c1*x), -c0*x - c1*x^3).
- Viscous dissipation → additive term proportional to -v; indicates exponential decay of amplitude when forcing is absent.
- Nonlinear dissipation/drag → terms like -v*Abs(v), -v**3; causes stronger damping at large |v| and can distort waveforms.
- Self-excitation (limit cycle) → damping coefficient changes sign with amplitude, e.g., (c0 - x**2)*v or (c0 - v**2)*v, producing sustained oscillations.
- Hardening/softening stiffness → presence of x**3 (or x*(c0 + c1*x**2)) implies amplitude-dependent frequency (backbone curve behavior).
- Pendulum/rotational oscillator behavior → sin(c*x) restoring suggests bounded angle dynamics and period increase with amplitude.
- External periodic drive → explicit sin/cos of t; expect resonance phenomena and steady-state response at the drive frequency.
- Parametric resonance → stiffness multiplied by (c0 + c1*cos(c2*t)) times x; instability bands and growth at specific modulation frequencies.
- Equilibrium shift / asymmetric potential → constant term or even-in-x components inside restoring force shift the stable point away from x=0.
- Non-separable nonlinear coupling → products like x*v or x**2*v indicate state-dependent damping/stiffness, often yielding asymmetric decay rates and waveform distortion.

With c9=−2.13 the rational denominator is (|x|−2.13)^3, implying a potential singularity near |x|≈2.13 (suggesting the term is only safe over a limited x-range); if |x| is far from 2.13 it behaves approximately like an additional linear-in-x correction. GT Equivalence Verification (PO5)
============================================================
GT: -beta*sin(v) - c0*beta*v - omega0**c1*(gamma*Abs(v)**c2 + c3)*x - omega0**c4*x**c5 - omega0**c6*x
Candidate formulas: 50

GT (fixed) is
\[
F(x,v)= -0.8961236228\,v\;-\;0.4480618114\sin(v)\;-\;1.2939539026\,x^3\;-\;1.2939539026\,x\big(0.09430567863|v|^{1/3}+1\big)\;-\;1.2939539026\,x.
\]
Key structural requirements:
- Has an explicit **\(\sin(v)\)** term (not \(\sin(\text{affine in }x)\), not \(\cos(t)\), etc.).
- Has a **fractional power damping** term **\(x\,|v|^{1/3}\)** (not log, not exp, not \(|v|\), not \(v|v|\), not \(|v|^3\)).
- No dependence on \(t\).
- Polynomial terms in \(x\): \(x^3\) and \(x\) (linear) with fixed coefficients; plus linear in \(v\).

All candidates are built from polynomials in \(x,v\), logs/exp of \(|v|\), and/or trig in \(t\) or \(x\). None contains \(\sin(v)\) as a standalone term, and none contains \(|v|^{1/3}\) multiplied by \(x\). Those two facts already block equivalence globally (for all real \(x,v,t\)).

Now candidate-by-candidate:

1. Uses \(x\log(\cdot)\), \(x\log(1+c|v|)\), rational in \(|x|\). No \(\sin(v)\). No \(|v|^{1/3}\). Cannot match.
2. Similar: has \(x\log\) terms and \(x|x|^{c}\). No \(\sin(v)\), no \(x|v|^{1/3}\). Cannot match.
3. Adds \(x^3\cos(c t)\). Any \(t\)-dependence must vanish ⇒ set that coefficient 0, but still no \(\sin(v)\) and no \(|v|^{1/3}\). Cannot match.
4. Has \(x\exp(c|v|)\) and \(x\cos(ct)\). Kill \(t\)-term by coefficient 0; still exp not fractional power, and no \(\sin(v)\). Cannot match.
5. Has \(x\exp(c|v|)\) and \(v\cos(ct)\). Kill \(t\)-term; still no \(\sin(v)\), no \(|v|^{1/3}\). Cannot match.
6. Has \(x\exp(c|v|)\), \(v|v|\), and \(v x^2\). None can become \(\sin(v)\) or \(x|v|^{1/3}\) for all real \(v\). Cannot match.
7. Has \(x\log\) terms and \(x^5\). No \(\sin(v)\), no fractional power. Cannot match.
8. Polynomial mix plus \(x\log(1+c v^2)\) and \(x\log(1+c|v|)\). Logs cannot equal \(|v|^{1/3}\) globally; no \(\sin(v)\). Cannot match.
9. Has \(x\log(1+c|v|)\), \(v\cos(ct)\), \(x\cos(ct)\). Must remove \(t\)-dependence; still no \(\sin(v)\), no \(|v|^{1/3}\). Cannot match.
10. Has constant offset \(c4\), \(x\log(1+c|v|)\), \(x\cos(ct)\), and \(vx\). GT has no constant term and no \(vx\). Even if set those to 0, still missing \(\sin(v)\) and \(|v|^{1/3}\). Cannot match.
11. Has \(x\exp(c|v|)\) and \(x\log(1+c v^2)\). No \(\sin(v)\), no \(|v|^{1/3}\). Cannot match.
12. Has \(x\exp(c|v|)\), \(v|v|\), \(x^5\). Not GT structure. Cannot match.
13. Has \(x\exp(c|v|)\), \(v|v|\), and \(v|v||x|\). Not GT. Cannot match.
14. Has \(x\log(1+c|v|)\) and \(x\cos(ct)\). Remove \(t\)-term; still log ≠ \(|v|^{1/3}\) globally and no \(\sin(v)\). Cannot match.
15. Has \(x\exp(c|v|)\) and \(v|v|\). No. Cannot match.

18. Same plus constant. Cannot match.

GT: -beta*sin(v) - c0*beta*v - omega0**c1*(gamma*Abs(v)**c2 + c3)*x - omega0**c4*x**c5 - omega0**c6*x

I need to analyze the Ground Truth (GT) and compare each candidate to it.

## Ground Truth Analysis

The GT numerical expression is:
```
-0.896123622766678*v - 1.29395390256765*x**3 - 1.29395390256765*x*(0.0943056786339846*Abs(v)**0.333333333333333 + 1) - 1.29395390256765*x - 0.448061811383339*sin(v)
```

Let me expand this:
- `-0.896123622766678*v`
- `-1.29395390256765*x**3`
- `-1.29395390256765*x*0.0943056786339846*Abs(v)**(1/3) - 1.29395390256765*x`
- `-1.29395390256765*x`
- `-0.448061811383339*sin(v)`

Combining the x terms:
- `-1.29395390256765*x - 1.29395390256765*x = -2.5879078051353*x`
- `-0.12202...*x*Abs(v)**(1/3)`

So GT = `-2.5879078051353*x - 1.29395390256765*x**3 - 0.122026...*x*Abs(v)**(1/3) - 0.896123622766678*v - 0.448061811383339*sin(v)`

The key basis functions in GT are:
1. `x` (linear)
2. `x**3`
3. `x*Abs(v)**(1/3)`
4. `v` (linear)
5. `sin(v)`

The critical function is **sin(v)**. This is a transcendental function that cannot be represented by polynomials in v (like v, v**3, v*Abs(v), etc.) or by other non-sinusoidal functions.

Also, `x*Abs(v)**(1/3)` is a specific basis function. Let me check what candidates could represent it.

## Key Observation

**sin(v)** is present in the GT. For a candidate to match, it must be able to produce a `sin(v)` term. Let me scan all candidates:

None of the candidates contain `sin(v)` explicitly. Some contain `sin(c7 + c8*x)` (Candidate 31), `cos(c9*t)` (various), `cos(c9*x)` (Candidate 43), but none have `sin(v)` or `cos(v)`.

Since `sin(v)` is linearly independent from all polynomial functions of v (like v, v**3, v*Abs(v)), exponential functions, logarithmic functions, etc., **no candidate can produce the sin(v) term**.

Let me verify: Could any candidate's terms combine to produce sin(v)?
- `v**3` terms: polynomial, cannot produce sin(v)
- `v*Abs(v)`: piecewise polynomial, cannot produce sin(v)
- `log(c*v**2+1)`: logarithmic, cannot produce sin(v)
- `log(c*Abs(v)+1)`: logarithmic, cannot produce sin(v)
- `exp(c*Abs(v))`: exponential, cannot produce sin(v)
- `cos(c*t)`: depends on t, not v
- `cos(c*x)`: depends on x, not v
- `sin(c7 + c8*x)`: depends on x, not v

None of these can produce `sin(v)`. The coefficient of sin(v) in GT is -0.448..., which is non-zero, so it cannot be ignored.

Therefore, **no candidate matches the GT**.
